## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x (restoring force), velocity v (damping), and possibly time t (external driving). Classical nonlinear oscillator equations include Duffing, Van der Pol, and parametrically driven systems.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (amplitude-dependent damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (forced nonlinear oscillator)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (linear forced oscillator)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (position-dependent stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-varying stiffness)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sign(v) (mixed damping model)
- General polynomial oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v (cross-coupled nonlinearity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope Γ¶Ê Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects Γ¶Ê Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay Γ¶Ê Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior Γ¶Ê Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects Γ¶Ê Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x┬│, xΓü╡) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium ΓÇË use odd polynomial in x
- Amplitude-dependent damping (e.g., (1-x┬▓)*v) indicates self-sustained oscillation (limit cycle) behavior ΓÇË Van der Pol structure
- If acceleration has no explicit time dependence, the system is autonomous and phase-plane analysis applies ΓÇË omit t
- Periodic explicit time dependence in acceleration (sin/cos of t) indicates external forcing ΓÇË include trigonometric functions of t
- Cross terms like x┬▓*v or x*v indicate nonlinear energy exchange between kinetic and potential modes
- Sign-preserving velocity terms (v┬│, v|v|) model nonlinear drag while maintaining correct dissipation direction
- Parametric excitation appears as multiplicative coupling between x and periodic functions of t
- If the system conserves energy (no v or t dependence), dv_dt must be expressible as -dU/dx for some potential U(x)
